planned change for an instance object into the set of\n526: // global planned changes.\n527: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) writeChange(ctx EvalContext, change *plans.ResourceInstanceChange, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the the caller.\n544: \t\tpanic(\"inconsistent address and/or deposed key in writeChange\")\n545: \t}\n546: \tif change.PrevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n547: \t\t// Should never happen, and a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n583: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n584: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := configVal.IsWhollyKnown()\n1751: \tdepsPending := n.dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx)\n1752: \t// If our configuration contains any unknown values, or we depend on any\n1753: \t// unknown values then we must defer the read to the apply phase by\n1754: \t// producing a \"Read\" change for this resource, and a placeholder value for\n1755: \t// it in the state.\n1756: \tif depsPending || !configKnown {\n1757: \t\t// We can't plan any changes if we're only refreshing, so the only\n1758: \t\t// value we can set here is whatever was in state previously.\n1759: \t\tif skipPlanChanges {\n1760: \t\t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1761: \t\t\t\tValue:  priorVal,\n1762: \t\t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1763: \t\t\t}\n1764: \n1765: \t\t\treturn nil, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1766: \t\t}\n1767: \n1768: \t\tvar reason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1769: \t\tswitch {\n1770: \t\tcase !configKnown:\n1771: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: \t\t\t// NOTE: depsPending can be true at the same time as configKnown\n1775: \t\t\t// is false; configKnown takes precedence because it's more\n1776: \t\t\t// specific.\n1777: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration is fully known, at least one dependency has changes pending\", n.Addr)\n1778: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseDependencyPending\n1779: \t\t}\n1780: \n1781: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal, configMarkPaths := configVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n1782: \t\tproposedNewVal := objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1783: \t\tproposedNewVal = proposedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1784: \n1785: \t\t// Apply detects that the data source will need to be read by the After\n1786: \t\t// value containing unknowns from PlanDataResourceObject.\n1787: \t\tplannedChange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1788: \t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1789: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1790: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1791: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1792: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1793: \t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1794: \t\t\t\tAfter:  proposedNewVal,\n1795: \t\t\t},\n1796: \t\t\tActionReason: reason,\n1797: \t\t}\n1798: \n1799: \t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1800: \t\t\tValue: addrs.NotDeposed, plans.Read, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n1806: \t\t}))\n1807: \n1808: \t\treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1809: \t}\n1810: \n1811: \t// We have a complete configuration with no dependencies to wait on, so we\n1812: \t// can read the data source into the state.\n1813: \tnewVal, readDiags := n.readDataSource(ctx, configVal)\n1814: \n1815: \t// Now we've loaded the data, and diags tells us whether we were successful\n1816: \t// or not, we are going to create our plannedChange and our\n1817: \t// proposedNewState.\n1818: \tvar plannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n1819: \tvar plannedNewState *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1820: \n1821: \t// If we are a nested block, then we want to create a plannedChange that\n1822: \t// tells \t// disguise that for a nested block. So,\n1835: \t\t// if we encountered an error we'll tidy up newVal so it makes sense\n1836: \t\t// and handle the error. If so, this resource will be loaded during both plan and apply\n1891: // operations to make sure the check is always giving the latest information.\n1892: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) nestedInCheckBlock() (*configs.Check, bool) {\n1893: \tif n.Config.Container != nil {\n1894: \t\tcheck, ok := n.Config.Container.(*configs.Check)\n1895: \t\treturn check, ok\n1896: \t}\n1897: \treturn nil, false\n1898: }\n1899: \n1900: // dependenciesHavePendingChanges determines whether any managed resource the\n1901: // receiver depends on has a change pending in the plan, in which case we'd\n1902: // need to override the usual behavior of immediately reading from the data\n1903: // source where possible, and instead defer the read until the apply step.\n1904: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx EvalContext) bool {\n1905: \tnModInst := n.Addr.Module\n1906: \tnMod := nModInst.Module()\n1907: \n1908: \t// Check and see if any depends_on dependencies have\n1909: \t// changes, since they won't show up as changes in the\n1910: \t// configuration.\n1911: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n1912: \n1913: \tdepsToUse := n.dependsOn\n1914: \n1915: \tif n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1916: \t\tif n.Config.HasCustomConditions() {\n1917: \t\t\t// For a data resource with custom conditions we need to look at\n1918: \t\t\t// the full set of resource dependencies -- both direct and\n1919: \t\t\t// indirect -- because an upstream update might be what's needed\n1920: \t\t\t// in order to make a condition pass.\n1921: \t\t\tdepsToUse = n.Dependencies\n1922: \t\t}\n1923: \t}\n1924: \n1925: \tfor _, d := range depsToUse {\n1926: \t\tif d.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1927: \t\t\t// Data sources have no external side effects, so they pose a need\n1928: \t\t\t// to delay this read. main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx evalApplyProvisioners determines if provisioners need to be run, and if so\n2056: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2057: // provisioning fails.\n2058: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: \t}\n2065: \tif when == configs.ProvisionerWhenCreate && !createNew {\n2066: \t\t// If we're not creating a new resource, then don't run provisioners\n2067: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) \t\tif p.When == when {\n2120: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2121: \t\t}\n2122: \t}\n2123: \n2124: \treturn result\n2125: }\n2126: \n2127: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the {\n2152: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] applyProvisioners: provisioning %s with %q\", n.Addr, prov.Type)\n2153: \n2154: \t\t// Get the provisioner\n2155: \t\tprovisioner, err := Otherwise, we'll continue using the\n2632: \t\t// prior state as the new value, making this effectively a no-op. resp.Private,\n2660: \t\t\tCreateBeforeDestroy: createBeforeDestroy,\n2661: \t\t}\n2662: \t\treturn newState, diags\n2663: \n2664: \tdefault:\n2665: \t\t// Non error case, were the object was // object associated with a resource instance. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CHmxJJ5pZ5fLBWfdptxAWX","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_016E1dN2E5iCsobwtXa2gaPJ","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes due to an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are applied across the planning pipeline. The root cause is that sensitivity marks from the provider schema are only applied during expression evaluation (GetResource), not when state is initially stored or refreshed, creating a mismatch between the before and after values in the plan comparison.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe phantom updates stem from an incomplete sensitivity mark workflow that spans four critical junctions:\n\n1. **State Serialization Gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go:98`): When a resource value is encoded to state, only existing sensitivity marks are captured via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`. Provider schema-defined sensitivity marks are never applied at this point, so `AttrSensitivePaths` in the stored state is incomplete.\n\n2. **Refresh Mark Reapplication** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:717-720`): After a provider refresh, only the marks that existed in the prior state are reapplied. Since schema marks were never stored, they don't get restored.\n\n3. **Compensating Workaround in Evaluation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`): The only place where schema-defined marks are applied to resource values is in `GetResource()` during config expression evaluation. For existing instances, the code unmasks the value, combines existing marks with schema marks via `schema.ValueMarks()`, then reapplies all marks.\n\n4. **Asymmetric Mark Comparison in Planning** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`): The plan method compares sensitivity marks between `plannedNewVal` (which has schema marks added during config evaluation) and `priorPaths` (which only has variable-reference marks from stored state). When these don't match, a NoOp action is changed to Update.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. State Serialization (instance_object.go)\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Only saves marks that are currently on the value\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // Lines 111-114: Schema marks are never captured here\n    src, err := ctyjson.Marshal(val, ty)\n    ...\n    // Line 131: AttrSensitivePaths only has variable-reference marks\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:      schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:          src,\n        AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,  // <-- INCOMPLETE: missing schema marks\n        ...\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n### 2. Refresh Mark Reapplication (node_resource_abstract_instance.go)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-722`\n\n```go\n// Lines 620-626: Unmarked prior value before sending to provider\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Lines 636-642: Provider returns unmarked response\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    PriorState:   priorVal,  // unmarked\n    ...\n})\n// resp.NewState also comes back unmarked\n\n// Lines 717-720: Only priorPaths are reapplied (schema marks missing)\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)  // <-- INCOMPLETE MARKS\n}\n```\n\n### 3. Compensating Marks in GetResource (evaluate.go)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`\n\n```go\n// Only location where schema marks are applied to resource values\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // <-- ADDS SCHEMA MARKS\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\nThis is called during config evaluation for resource references, creating schema marks that don't exist in state.\n\n### 4. Asymmetric Mark Comparison in Plan (node_resource_abstract_instance.go)\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1199-1210`\n\n```go\n// Line 1208: The exact mechanism of phantom updates\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update  // <-- TRIGGERED BY MARK MISMATCH\n}\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `plannedNewVal`: Has marks from config evaluation (includes schema marks via GetResource)\n- `priorPaths`: Only has marks from prior state (no schema marks, because they were never stored)\n- `unmarkedPaths`: Config-level marks captured before sending to provider\n\n### 5. The root cause is that sensitivity marks from the provider schema are only applied during expression evaluation (GetResource), not when state is initially stored or refreshed, creating a mismatch between the before and after values in the plan comparison.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe phantom updates stem from an incomplete sensitivity mark workflow that spans four critical junctions:\n\n1. **State Serialization Gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go:98`): When a resource value is encoded to state, only existing sensitivity marks are captured via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`. Provider schema-defined sensitivity marks are never applied at this point, so `AttrSensitivePaths` in the stored state is incomplete.\n\n2. **Refresh Mark Reapplication** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:717-720`): After a provider refresh, only the marks that existed in the prior state are reapplied. Since schema marks were never stored, they don't get restored.\n\n3. **Compensating Workaround in Evaluation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`): The only place where schema-defined marks are applied to resource values is in `GetResource()` during config expression evaluation.
